  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5b2b36f0-c216-4b0e-b8fb-bc5aecbb7766'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

Luis Bernardo is ill-prepared for the challenges of plantation life – used to a softer urban existence, he is shocked by the conditions under which the workers labour.<br /><br />But with the English closing in on São Tomé’s cocoa plantations, the island’s main means of survival, Luis Bernardo must endeavour to protect the island and its community.</span>

<a href="/questions/807576-is-it-a-single-p-o-v-book-what-is-the">Is it a single p.o.v book? 
What is the book about, theme-wise?</a>
</div>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/51324083-margarida"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1452389114i/51324083._UY100_CR25,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/51324083-margarida">Margarida</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Set in the beginning of the 20th century, it's about a young businessman, Luís Bernardo Valença, from Lisbon who is invited by the King to be Governor<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Set in the beginning of the 20th century, it's about a young businessman, Luís Bernardo Valença, from Lisbon who is invited by the King to be Governor of Portugal's smallest colony - Sao Tomé and Principe (2 islands in the African Atlantic Coast, near the Equator). He is sent there with a single purpose - to prove to the British council, David Jameson, that there are no slaves in the coffee and cocoa plantations of Sao Tomé. Unfortunately, he will meet across the island several plantation owners to whom the terms "humane conditions" mean very little and whose definition of "free workers" is wider than usual. So, how will he convince the council of something he is not sure is true?<br />Luis Bernardo eventually befriends David, but at the same time falls is love with his wife Ann, and thus the fate of the diplomatic relations between England and Portugal rest on the hands of these 3 characters.<br /><br />The story is mostly told from Luis Bernardo's p.o.v., though the author also gifts us with the story of how David's career got him from India to S. Tome, from David's p.o.v.<br /><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_821399624" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/821399624" />
    <a title="Daniel Gamboa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4454327-daniel-gamboa"><img alt="Daniel Gamboa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489305311p2/4454327.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/821399624?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel Gamboa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel Gamboa" href="/user/show/4454327-daniel-gamboa">Daniel Gamboa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780747596622" href="/book/show/7729173-equator">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer821399624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8973082714808162258">I was motivated to read this novel for an upcoming trip I am doing this Summer to Sao Tome. It was recommended in my Bradt Guide to Sao Tome & Principe, and this is one of the two novels available in English set in this African country. I am very glad I read it, for there is little information available about this country other than the basics offered by geography and history books.<br/><br/>Luis Bernardo Valenca is a Portuguese, hedonist man living in Lisbon at the beginning of the 1900's. David Jameson,</span>
  <span id="freeText8973082714808162258" style="display:none">I was motivated to read this novel for an upcoming trip I am doing this Summer to Sao Tome. It was recommended in my Bradt Guide to Sao Tome &amp; Principe, and this is one of the two novels available in English set in this African country. I am very glad I read it, for there is little information available about this country other than the basics offered by geography and history books.<br /><br />Luis Bernardo Valenca is a Portuguese, hedonist man living in Lisbon at the beginning of the 1900's. David Jameson, and his wife, Ann, are a British, passionate couple living in India. When the British accuse Portugal of keeping slavery in Sao Tome &amp; Principe, King Dom Carlos of Portugal asks Luis Bernardo to become the governor of this Portuguese colony. His mission is to prove to David Jameson, sent to Sao Tome as a British council, that the Angolan workers in Sao Tome &amp; Principe are being treated as any other Portuguese citizens. However, will Luis Bernardo accomplish convincing the British council of this? Will Luis Bernardo's ideas about colonialism fit in within the local community of Portuguese cocoa planters? Will Luis Bernardo be able to abandon his comfortable life of pleasures in Lisbon and settle down in a backwater, African colony? This is "Equator", and while most of the time this is a gripping novel, there a few elements that made me give it four stars instead of five:<br /><br />1. At times, it switches from fiction to non-fiction very easily. This sometimes made me feel I was reading a text book about history and not a historical novel. I wish the author had been more subtle with this. It was always interesting to read about it and it gave historical context to understand why things were happening, but it made the plot stop in order to make room for the history classes. However, this did not happen often, but when it did, I could not help wondering what had happened to the plot.<br /><br />2. The author is skilled at giving you a sense of place, but sometimes he fails. There are many beautiful passages, specially those about loneliness and those about Sao Tome, among others, but other times he is good at just listing and numbering. Mentioning names of places, and names of objects, without descriptions, does not give a sense of place, and, for me, reading lists is pointless and easy to forget. However, like I said, when he describes, rather than just name, he is good at it, and those descriptions have stayed within me even after I read the novel.<br /><br />3. I wish the author had had more confidence in the readers at remembering things. Whenever he mentioned something he had previously talked about, he felt he needed to give you a brief summary of the issue again, and this became annoying at times because I felt I was reading about some issues even more than twice. This also had me reading very long sentences, which lost sense by the time I finish reading them.<br /><br />However, all in all, this is great novel. Reading about Sao Tome &amp; Principe, Portugal and India was always interesting, and the twists and turns of the plot kept me intrigued as to what was going to happen next all the time. Another great, historical novel, this time about the Portuguese colony of Goa, I can recommend is Lino Leitao's "The Gift of the Holy Cross".</span>
  <a data-text-id="8973082714808162258" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3409180571" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3409180571" />
    <a title="Luís" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/117399210-lu-s"><img alt="Luís" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598708286p2/117399210.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3409180571?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luís" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luís" href="/user/show/117399210-lu-s">Luís</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789895550135" href="/book/show/2373424.Equador">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/117399210-lu-s?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/117399210-lu-s?shelf=portuguese-literature">portuguese-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/117399210-lu-s?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3409180571" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1014809553936667385">The novel by Miguel Sousa Tavares, Ecuador, is the story of Luis Bernardo Valença, a young Lisbon dandy who is offered by King Don Carlos a post he cannot refuse. That of the governor of a Portuguese colony in off Africa, in Sao Tome and Principe which he knows nothing abroad. A bit like most Portuguese at the beginning of the 20th century, moreover. Its mission is to refute the idea that the English have concerning this tiny archipelago far from its metropolis, namely that slavery practised the</span>
  <span id="freeText1014809553936667385" style="display:none">The novel by Miguel Sousa Tavares, Ecuador, is the story of Luis Bernardo Valença, a young Lisbon dandy who is offered by King Don Carlos a post he cannot refuse. That of the governor of a Portuguese colony in off Africa, in Sao Tome and Principe which he knows nothing abroad. A bit like most Portuguese at the beginning of the 20th century, moreover. Its mission is to refute the idea that the English have concerning this tiny archipelago far from its metropolis, namely that slavery practised there, illegally since it has abolished since 1876, under cover of false employment contracts.<br />Luis, who led a life made up of bourgeois receptions and an impossible love with Mathilde, a married woman, therefore sees himself embarked far from his landmarks and far from the splendour of Lisbon, to save the honour of his homeland. This fact is how the King agreed to accept this mission. There, he discovers a world that is both fascinating, that an island of wild, dazzling nature, but also cruel, of a world in which forced labour still practised there. He tried in vain to accomplish his mission there with wealthy owners of coffee and cocoa plantations who naturally did not wish to see their way of life threatened by this young civil servant whom they found too cumbersome.<br />From then on, he made a series of visits and receptions to get to know these islands and these wealthy owners whom he administered in the name of the King. Very quickly, he realizes that the truth about what is happening in these plantations hidden from him. He is also intimidated so that he does not reveal the indecent practices done to Africans.<br />Shortly after his arrival, the English consul arrives accompanied by his young wife with bewitching charms. His presence in Sao Tome and Principe, he owes it to his penchant for gambling. Indeed, then promised to a brilliant career in the British colonies, one discovers to him this vice which stains his reputation of the intractable official. This fact is how he has no other choice, to save his honour and that of his couple than to embark far from the Indies where he stationed there. His wife, who has sworn never to abandon him, finds herself also forced to follow him.<br />David and Bartolomeu, therefore, find themselves in this colony with each mission to report on workers' situation on the island to their respective sovereign. One was defending the Portuguese crown, the other the British crown which threatened to boycott products from the island if forced labour was confirmed there. Very quickly, the English couple would befriend this coveted young bachelor, although they opposed in their mission. And both, enamoured of the liberalism of the time, agreed on the fact that the plantation workers are under duress and have no possibility of returning home, to Angola, once their 5-year contract has ended. Now, how can one tell the King of Portugal that England is right? And how do you convince plantation owners to change their way of life? And how could he persuade his friend the consul that telling the truth in his report for the crown of England would threaten his mission, his post and the esteem he had with the King of Portugal?</span>
  <a data-text-id="1014809553936667385" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_360485453" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/360485453" />
    <a title="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship"><img alt="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325201543p2/5229326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/360485453?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship" href="/user/show/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship">Emma Deplores Goodreads Censorship</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780747581741" href="/book/show/2237673.Equator">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=world-books-challenge">world-books-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=read-in-translation">read-in-translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=africa">africa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5229326-emma-deplores-goodreads-censorship?shelf=sao-tome-and-principe">sao-tome-and-principe</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer360485453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14785098703110275713">I was excited to find a book set in São Tomé and Príncipe, and this one started out interesting, albeit slow-paced. Unfortunately, it soon became offensive on several levels, and took much longer than I expected to finish.<br/><br/>In 1905, Luis Bernardo is a gentleman in Lisbon when he's called upon to spend three years as governor of São Tomé and Príncipe. The British are accusing the Portuguese of using slave labor on the islands, and threatening to boycott their exports; Luis Bernardo's job is to clea</span>
  <span id="freeText14785098703110275713" style="display:none">I was excited to find a book set in São Tomé and Príncipe, and this one started out interesting, albeit slow-paced. Unfortunately, it soon became offensive on several levels, and took much longer than I expected to finish.<br /><br />In 1905, Luis Bernardo is a gentleman in Lisbon when he's called upon to spend three years as governor of São Tomé and Príncipe. The British are accusing the Portuguese of using slave labor on the islands, and threatening to boycott their exports; Luis Bernardo's job is to clean up the situation before that happens. (Note that while the international relations aspect is historical, Luis Bernardo is fictional. Unfortunately, the author does not include a note at the end explaining how much of his story was inspired by real events.)<br /><br />As I mentioned, the story, while it moves slowly, is at least interesting: Luis Bernardo is immediately at odds with the reactionary plantation society, and his efforts to reform it kept my attention. It's not often that novels about slavery feature a character in authority actively trying to change things. The white male characters, including Luis Bernardo, are reasonably well-drawn; the resistance that he meets feels genuine and realistic. The islands come across fairly vividly, and the novel appears well-researched and contains interesting historical information.<br /><br />But of course, there's something wrong with a novel where only the white male characters come across as fully human, and the number of -isms Tavares manages to pack into the book fairly boggles the mind. First, the women: they exist entirely as sex objects and accessories, without any development beyond that; this is particularly unfortunate with Ann, who gets a lot of page time but never becomes more than an "ample, panting bosom." In fact, there's only one woman in the book with whom Luis Bernardo does not have sex, and that's only because he doesn't get around to it.<br /><br />Second, the Africans: they're Hollywood stereotypes, none of them taking important roles, even though their conditions are at the heart of the book. This is especially odd because a crucial aspect of Luis Bernardo's character is that he's the one Portuguese on São Tomé who sees and treats them as human--one wonders why the author couldn't manage to do the same.<br /><br />Relatedly, there's the treatment of colonialism. Given the setting, it's natural enough for the (white) cast to support it; even the more liberal-minded Luis Bernardo is in favor as long as it's "civilizing." But things really get ugly when the omniscient narrator starts talking about India: the book states flat-out that the local people are incapable of governing themselves, the British are good colonialists who don't meddle and are doing them a service, etc. And it reverts to stereotypes, contrasting that "elemental, instinctive" country with the "civilised world where good taste and discrimination reigned." Tavares even gives us this howler: "It was arguable whether Providence had chosen Great Britain to direct the destinies of India: after all, the Portuguese had got there first and, after them, and before the English, the French." Around this point, I started to suspect that the 2003 publication date was misleading: perhaps the book was written contemporaneously with the events it describes, but published posthumously? Sadly, no. Somehow this really is a 21st century novel.<br /><br />To top it off, Tavares even throws in some anti-Semitism: an antiques dealer is demonized as a "despicable Jewish trader" and the like, for the terrible crime of complaining when an item he paid a large amount of money for in a legitimate sale is publicly confiscated by the police as stolen property.<br /><br />At any rate, there's a reasonably interesting story in there somewhere, but I'm not about to recommend a book that reduces most of humanity to objects. Again, this is especially unfortunate here because in the hands of a better author, these characters and this story might have amounted to something worthwhile.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14785098703110275713" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_788150347" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/788150347" />
    <a title="Siria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/115473-siria"><img alt="Siria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332731316p2/115473.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/788150347?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Siria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Siria" href="/user/show/115473-siria">Siria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780747596622" href="/book/show/7729173-equator">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/115473-siria?shelf=21st-century">21st-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/115473-siria?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/115473-siria?shelf=portuguese-fiction">portuguese-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer788150347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9600617669421384351"><i>Equator</i> began promisingly, introducing Luis Bernardo Valenca, the owner of a small Portuguese shipping company who in 1905 is himself unwillingly shipped off to the other side of the globe to be governor of the tiny cocoa-producing colony of Sao Tome e Principe. Luis has been tasked by the king of Portugal with persuading the Portuguese colonists on the island to forego slave labour, while at the same time persuading the visiting English consul that slavery has never existed there. Tavares' init</span>
  <span id="freeText9600617669421384351" style="display:none"><i>Equator</i> began promisingly, introducing Luis Bernardo Valenca, the owner of a small Portuguese shipping company who in 1905 is himself unwillingly shipped off to the other side of the globe to be governor of the tiny cocoa-producing colony of Sao Tome e Principe. Luis has been tasked by the king of Portugal with persuading the Portuguese colonists on the island to forego slave labour, while at the same time persuading the visiting English consul that slavery has never existed there. Tavares' initial description of early twentieth century Portugal and its political situation are intriguing, but much of the rest of the novel is disappointing and at points frankly racist. <br /><br />Tavares has written yet another novel about slavery and colonialism in Africa which mostly elides African people and their experiences in favour of focusing on white men. It's a racism which isn't overt, but which cannot seem to conceive of a world in which the most important things that happen don't involve white men. Much of the central portion of the novel, when I was anticipating that Tavares would really get to grips with what was happening on Sao Tome, shifted to a lengthy (an Orientalising) description of India in order to give the back story of another white male character. There was really no need to give this back story at such detailed length, and it seemed to have been included only so that we could see how colonial service had done another white man wrong—and he's one of the good guys, really! He speaks Hindi and Urdu so he can't be racist, and when he feels up members of a rajah's harem he only ever does so over their clothes and never puts his penis in their vaginas so it's totally not the same as cheating, you guys! Ugh. <br /><br />Non-white characters have only a handful of lines in <i>Equator</i>, despite a slave rebellion being one of the climactic events of the novel; character development for the handful of women in the book mostly comes in the form of descriptions of their breasts and in how willing they are to jump into bed with Luis. An example of how white people should not approach writing historical fiction.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9600617669421384351" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3480761252?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gonçalo Diniz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gonçalo Diniz" href="/user/show/68293965-gon-alo-diniz">Gonçalo Diniz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3480761252" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3704222898992027873">What to say about this book? For starters, all I knew of it going in was that it's a Portuguese book set in Africa.<br/>It was a very enjoyable read despite some long exposition info dumps. The author writes very well and the plot is interesting. The setting is the 1905 Portuguese colony São Tomé and Príncipe and the diplomatic war between Portugal and England on whether slavery is still happening in the colony.<br/>We follow Luís Bernardo, a Portuguese lawyer somewhat bored with life and who happens to b</span>
  <span id="freeText3704222898992027873" style="display:none">What to say about this book? For starters, all I knew of it going in was that it's a Portuguese book set in Africa.<br />It was a very enjoyable read despite some long exposition info dumps. The author writes very well and the plot is interesting. The setting is the 1905 Portuguese colony São Tomé and Príncipe and the diplomatic war between Portugal and England on whether slavery is still happening in the colony.<br />We follow Luís Bernardo, a Portuguese lawyer somewhat bored with life and who happens to be chosen by the king himself due to an article he wrote to act as the Islands' governor. His mission is to prove there is no slavery in the colony and the story develops from there.<br />However, and maybe because I was in a reading slump, the story takes its sweet time starting, which may lead some to think it's boring. For the greater part, it's not, although some points here and there could've been shortened (unnecessary long long chapters).<br />I think every Portuguese who likes to read should take a peak at this book, and given the current social times, it's very curious to see the way black folk were treated in the beginning of the last century vs what's happening now. It has also been translated into English, Spanish, French, Italian and other languages, so my foreign followers can also read it.<br />Overall, enjoyable, 3.5 ⭐<br />P.S.: Mild mild spoiler, the book has some R-rated romance in it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3704222898992027873" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_757359326" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/757359326" />
    <a title="Henna Pääkkönen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15721719-henna-p-kk-nen"><img alt="Henna Pääkkönen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466145781p2/15721719.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/757359326?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Henna Pääkkönen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Henna Pääkkönen" href="/user/show/15721719-henna-p-kk-nen">Henna Pääkkönen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15721719-henna-p-kk-nen?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15721719-henna-p-kk-nen?shelf=historic-fiction">historic-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer757359326" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10669976792367089525">Miguel Sousa Tavares´first novel relates the complicated political situation of Säo Tomé and Principe islands (a Portuguese colony at the time) along the west coast of Africa in the beginning of 1900´s. <br/>The main character of this historic novel is Luis Bernardo Valença, who owns his own shipping agency in Lisbon, likes to read his daily papers, has an interest in politics and occasionally publicly comments some newspaper articles such as the one recently on the colony of Säo Tomé and Principe. <br/>L</span>
  <span id="freeText10669976792367089525" style="display:none">Miguel Sousa Tavares´first novel relates the complicated political situation of Säo Tomé and Principe islands (a Portuguese colony at the time) along the west coast of Africa in the beginning of 1900´s. <br />The main character of this historic novel is Luis Bernardo Valença, who owns his own shipping agency in Lisbon, likes to read his daily papers, has an interest in politics and occasionally publicly comments some newspaper articles such as the one recently on the colony of Säo Tomé and Principe. <br />Luis Bernardo lives his enjoyable life in Lisbon “high-society” in the beginning of the 1900´s when, out of the blue, he is called by King D. Carlos for a meeting at the royal summer palace in Vila Viçosa. The king posts Luis Bernardo into special mission as the governor of the Säo Tomé &amp; Principe islands along the Equator, by the coast of Western Africa. <br />The humid and tropic island of Säo Tomé was far from the Lisbon that Luis Bernardo knew, and had a population of 45.000 and no cars. This Portuguese colony was mainly cultivating cocoa and coffee (and some sugar) since the 16th century, with the help of the slaves that had been brought in from African mainland (mostly Angola). By 1908, Säo Tomé had become the world´s largest producer of cocoa, and the supposedly continued slavery in the islands became a topic of international controversy especially since Portugal had officially abolished slavery in 1876. <br />Luis Bernardo was to take up his position as the governor of this colony, and was to prove to the international community (especially England) that the Angolan workers working at the cocoa farms were not slaves and this way, avoid the boycotts by the English and German companies....<br />As Luis Bernardo sails on the “Zaire” through the fog to his now home along the equator, his despair and longing for civilization and Lisbon life (the life he had known so far) can be touched and felt through the beautiful writing of Miguel Sousa Tavares….<br />I loved the book, besides an interesting history lesson for me, it took me back to the beginning of 1900´s and to the equator. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10669976792367089525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11242038998936358005">This novel is a compelling reading mainly because of the historical context.<br/>Set in a period near the end of Portugal's Monarchy and where its colonies were used as political weapons by old (so called) allies, Tavares presents us with the typical romantic tale of torn hearts.   <span id="freeText11242038998936358005" style="display:none">This novel is a compelling reading mainly because of the historical context.<br />Set in a period near the end of Portugal's Monarchy and where its colonies were used as political weapons by old (so called) allies, Tavares presents us with the typical romantic tale of torn hearts. In these romantic context, nothing new is presented and the ending becomes obvious before the last pages.<br />What's most interesting in this book, as said previously, is the historic context where the novel takes place with all its political intricacies as well as the geographic location, specially because these aspects match some gaps in my knowledge of my own country's history.<br />A must read for the historical curious due to its amount of details, even if the romantic parts can be rather dull.<br /></span>

<div id="review_811301159" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/811301159" />
    <a title="Mariana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2686791-mariana"><img alt="Mariana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1251890188p2/2686791.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mariana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mariana" href="/user/show/2686791-mariana">Mariana</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer811301159" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15123276798718167730">Sousa Tavares is a very good descriptive writer, a keen observer of nature and society, who manages to convey the light and dark of Santo Tomé without falling into the (to me mightily annoying) traps of costumbrism. Emotions are his weakness, though: the passion between Luis and his beloved felt flat and unbelievable.<br/>Still an enjoyable book and a worth read for its human portrait of colonialism in the early XX century.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer993158991" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9792042173452480960">The setting for most of this book is São Tomé and Príncipe in 1905. It reads as if it might have been written then, although it was actually written in the C21st and the author is Portuguese. It evokes the time and place well. The main character thinks and acts the way someone of his time and background would.<br/>It is also a good story, which made me want to keep reading. Other commitments got in the way and I did not finish the book, but I will return to it.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2128889077" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2128889077" />
    <a title="R.L." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46340789-r-l"><img alt="R.L." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441732921p2/46340789.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2128889077?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="R.L." class="user" itemprop="url" name="R.L." href="/user/show/46340789-r-l">R.L.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2128889077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16449084048852533981">Κριτική στα Ελληνικά από κάτω....<br/><br/>Equator is a very interesting book, touching on many different subjects. Unfortunately, it doesn't avoid many clichés with some stereotypical behaviors and characters, but I really "enjoyed" the historical setting and some of the plot elements. How many people are familiar with São Tomé and Príncipe and/or Portuguese politics on early 1900s anyway? This book intrigued me to seek further information on those.<br/><br/><br/><br/>Ενδιαφέρον βιβλίο που στην αρχή βρήκα υπερβολικά αργόσυρ</span>
  <span id="freeText16449084048852533981" style="display:none">Κριτική στα Ελληνικά από κάτω....<br /><br />Equator is a very interesting book, touching on many different subjects. Unfortunately, it doesn't avoid many clichés with some stereotypical behaviors and characters, but I really "enjoyed" the historical setting and some of the plot elements. How many people are familiar with São Tomé and Príncipe and/or Portuguese politics on early 1900s anyway? This book intrigued me to seek further information on those.<br /><br /><br /><br />Ενδιαφέρον βιβλίο που στην αρχή βρήκα υπερβολικά αργόσυρτο αλλά σιγά-σιγά άρχισε να μου αρέσει πιο πολύ. Ο ρυθμός παραμένει υπερβολικά αργός βέβαια και δεν αποφεύγονται τα κλισέ και οι υπερβολές, ωστόσο νομίζω το μεγάλο του ατού είναι η χρονική περίοδος και τα μέρη που διαδραματίζεται η ιστορία. <br /><br />Για κάποιο λόγο το Ελληνικό αναγνωστικό κοινό είναι πιο εξοικειωμένο με την ιστορία της Λατινικής Αμερικής και με την Ισπανία, με την αποικιοκρατία των Άγγλων στην Ινδία, ίσως με των Αγγλογάλλων στην Βόρεια Αφρική, αλλά όχι και τόσο με την ιστορία της Πορτογαλίας ή την αποικιοκρατία σε άλλα σημεία του κόσμου.<br />Για εμένα ίσως το μεγαλύτερο πλεονέκτημα του βιβλίου ήταν αυτό: Ότι με έβαλε στην διαδικασία να ψάξω και να μάθω περισσότερα για αυτά τα δύο νησάκια που ήταν αποικίες της Πορτογαλίας μέχρι πριν 4 δεκαετίες και μου άνοιξε την όρεξη να ψάξω πιο πολλά στοιχεία σχετικά με την πολιτική κατάσταση στην Πορτογαλία των αρχών του 20 αιώνα.<br />Ειλικρινά τώρα, πόσοι από εμάς θα μπορούσαμε να δείξουμε τα Σάο Τομέ και Πρίνσιπε στον χάρτη ή να προσθέσουμε οποιαδήποτε πληροφορία για αυτά πριν την ανάγνωση του βιβλίου;<br /><br />Αυτός λοιπόν ήταν ο ένας κύριος θεματικός άξονας του βιβλίου. Ο τόπος - το τοπίο και οι άνθρωποι που κατοικούσαν εκεί και ο τρόπος ζωής-. Το άλλο ήταν οι διαφορετικές απόψεις περί δουλείας, ο ρατσισμός, το εμπόριο, τα συμφέροντα των χωρών, το πολιτικό πλαίσιο και οι διεθνής συσχετισμοί, η άσκηση πολιτικής, η μικροπολιτική, η διπλωματία και η πολιτική ίντριγκα. Ευχαριστήθηκα αρκετά και αυτό το μέρος του βιβλίου, αν και κάποιες στροφές της πλοκής δεν είναι και πολλοί πιστευτές.<br /><br />Ο τρίτος άξονας, είναι οι κυρίως ήρωες, οι μεταξύ τους σχέσεις και πως αυτές οι προσωπικές σχέσεις εξελίσσονται και επηρεάζουν την μεγαλύτερη εικόνα. Ενδιαφέρουσα η ιστορία και εδώ αν και όχι χωρίς αρνητικά σημεία.<br /><br />Αυτές οι τρεις πλευρές του βιβλίου δεν είναι ανεξάρτητες η μία από την άλλη και συχνά θαύμασα την ικανότητα του συγγραφέα να γράψει ένα τόσο πολύπλευρο βιβλίο.<br /><br />Ωστόσο συχνά ο συγγραφέας με απογοήτευσε επίσης. Αρχικά το βιβλίο πλατειάζει αρκετά στα πρώτα κεφάλαια με περιγραφές κάποιων στοιχείων που δεν χρησιμεύουν πουθενά στην συνέχεια, ενώ δεν είναι πειστικός ο τρόπος που ο κεντρικός ήρωας, ο Λουίς Μπερνάρντο αποφασίζει να δεχτεί την πρόταση που θα του αλλάξει την ζωή. Στην συνέχεια, οι χαρακτήρες του βιβλίου στο νησί γίνονται αφόρητα κλισέ και η αφήγηση αρκετά μονόπλευρη, ωστόσο εκεί που το μυθιστόρημα βρίσκει έναν ρυθμό, ξαφνικά ο συγγραφέας μας μεταφέρει σε εντελώς άλλο τόπο, στην Ινδία για να μας γνωρίσει τους άλλους βασικούς χαρακτήρες, τον Δαυίδ και την Ανν. <br />Νομίζω ότι σε αυτό το σημείο το βιβλίο κάνει μια μεγάλη παρένθεση που δεν ήταν απαραίτητη και όταν πια οι τρεις τους συναντιούνται και ο συγγραφέας ξαναπιάνει την κεντρική αφήγηση, αρχίζουν οι πολλές υπερβολές. Αν και ως ένα βαθμό το ψυχογράφημα των τριών τους είναι πειστικό, οι μεταξύ τους σχέσεις, η συμπεριφορά τους εν έτη 1906 και η εν γένη πορεία τους είναι υπερβολική. Δεν θέλω να γράψω σπόιλερ, αλλά πολλά σημεία της πλοκής φαίνονται να έρχονται από το πουθενά και να καταλήγουν στο πουθενά.<br /><br />Προς το τέλος, το βιβλίο γίνεται απλά προβλέψιμο και "φτηνό", όταν κάποια γεγονότα παίρνουν δραματικές διαστάσεις και οι ήρωες δρουν με τρόπο δυσανάλογο με την ποιότητα του χαρακτήρα τους που έχει σκιαγραφήσει ο Ταβάρες ως τότε. Θα περίμενα κάτι καλύτερο από τον συγγραφέα.<br /><br />Σίγουρα ένα ατμοσφαιρικό ιστορικό μυθιστόρημα, κάτι ξεχωριστό από τα συνηθισμένα. Αξίζει να το διαβάσετε και να σχηματίσετε δική σαν γνώμη...<br /><br />ΥΓ: Θα πρέπει να πω ότι εκνευρίστηκα λιγάκι με τις Εκδόσεις Ενάλιος. Υπάρχουν πάρα πολλά τυπογραφικά και συντακτικά λάθη και σε κάνα-δυο σημεία το κείμενο δεν βγάζει νόημα, προφανώς λόγω της δυσκολίας απόδοσης κάποιων εκφράσεων από τα Πορτογαλικά στα Ελληνικά. Αισθάνθηκα μια προχειρότητα και μια αδιαφορία για τον αναγνώστη/αγοραστή του βιβλίου. Είμαι άσχετη με το πως δουλεύουν οι εκδοτικού οίκοι, ωστόσο δεν έχουν ανθρώπους να ελέγχουν το κείμενο πριν πάει προς εκτύπωση και να επιλύουν τέτοια θέματα;<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16449084048852533981" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2883526408" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2883526408" />
    <a title="Rafael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/95581426-rafael"><img alt="Rafael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602883014p2/95581426.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2883526408?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rafael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rafael" href="/user/show/95581426-rafael">Rafael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2883526408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2095144171510021820">In 1905, Luis Bernardo is a typical bon-vivant of the high society of Lisbon when he is invited to spend three years as governor of the colony of São Tomé and Príncipe, two "islets" in the middle of the ocean as the author likes to emphasize. The British are accusing the Portuguese of using slave labor on the islands and threatening to boycott their exports; Luis Bernardo's job is to clear the situation before that happens. (Note that Luis Bernardo is fictitious).<br/><br/>Ecuador is a very interesting hi</span>
  <span id="freeText2095144171510021820" style="display:none">In 1905, Luis Bernardo is a typical bon-vivant of the high society of Lisbon when he is invited to spend three years as governor of the colony of São Tomé and Príncipe, two "islets" in the middle of the ocean as the author likes to emphasize. The British are accusing the Portuguese of using slave labor on the islands and threatening to boycott their exports; Luis Bernardo's job is to clear the situation before that happens. (Note that Luis Bernardo is fictitious).<br /><br />Ecuador is a very interesting historical novel. The author shares a lot of information about the political situation in São Tomé and Portugal in the early 1900s (the end of the Portuguese monarchy), moving from fiction to nonfiction very easily and proving that he did a lot of historical research to write the book - at some points this narrative is more than enough, and sometimes underestimates the reader by mentioning things he had previously spoken. However, the characters are very well built, the story flows, the scenes are extremely rich in details.<br /><br />Unfortunately, and here is the critical point of the book, the author didn't avoid many clichés with some behaviors and stereotyped characters. I would attribute this to the fact that it’s a white author approach writing of historical slave fiction, which results in only a few lines in the book dedicated to nonwhite characters - although a slave rebellion is one of the climaxes of the novel. If the nonwhite characters had got more attention, I believe the story would be better.<br /><br />Anyway, I really enjoyed the historical setting and some of the plot twists, which left me intrigued to move forward. * Was really nice have the pleasure to read the book in the original language (Portuguese❤️).</span>
  <a data-text-id="2095144171510021820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3013558115" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3013558115" />
    <a title="Rosie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23493632-rosie"><img alt="Rosie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1381506323p2/23493632.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3013558115?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rosie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rosie" href="/user/show/23493632-rosie">Rosie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780747581741" href="/book/show/2237673.Equator">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23493632-rosie?shelf=read-round-the-world">read-round-the-world</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3013558115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3419648462819172922">I was very happy to find a historical novel set on Sao Tome and Principe, islands off the coast of West Africa which I had never heard of before: formerly Portuguese colonies, producers of large amounts of cocoa. This novel is about the governor who in 1905 was sent to attempt to put an end to slavery on the islands (labourers were shipped there from Portuguese Angola). It is well researched and the descriptions of life on the islands, its climate and scenery, and the historical events are very </span>
  <span id="freeText3419648462819172922" style="display:none">I was very happy to find a historical novel set on Sao Tome and Principe, islands off the coast of West Africa which I had never heard of before: formerly Portuguese colonies, producers of large amounts of cocoa. This novel is about the governor who in 1905 was sent to attempt to put an end to slavery on the islands (labourers were shipped there from Portuguese Angola). It is well researched and the descriptions of life on the islands, its climate and scenery, and the historical events are very well done. It is unfortunate that the descriptions of the Angolan people, even being portrayed as they are through the eyes of the sympathetic main character, are still quite demeaning, although I suppose he was trying to write the thought processes of a man of the period. As others have pointed out the author's treatment of women is also pretty sexist (with a couple of graphic sex scenes, eye-roll). So I have mixed feelings about the book and whether I would recommend it to others - but it is a fascinating story, and I am glad to have learned about this small part of the history of these remote, now independent African islands. I would love to visit them one day!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3419648462819172922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('exxP0Lg85CU8jiqLEi5Pl4s+904qJVLmnVYIHuY5vwPp1+wDLCX5NMDntAeEine3AgSMPrRBx8sRKKeom+vg4A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8YC4PEE6AIkBiRpUhiMal3ORVRvRoflCc84I6AuOHopjSxvv1SMdmP3ghNgQhyK3+qsua0/FbG//sKdedlxBaQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

O livro foi publicado no Porto em 1888. A acção de Os Maias passa-se em Lisboa, na segunda metade do século XIX, e apresenta-nos a história de três gerações da família Maia. A acção inicia-se no Outono de 1875, quando Afonso da Maia, nobre e pobre proprietário, se instala no Ramalhete com o neto recém formado em Medicina. Neste momento faz-se uma longa descrição da casa - &quot;O Ramalhete,&quot; cujo nome tem origem num painel de azulejos com um ramo de girassóis, e não em algo fresco ou campestre, tal como o nome nos remete a pensar. Afonso da Maia era o personagem mais simpático do romance e aquele que o autor mais valorizou, pois não se lhe conhecem defeitos. É um homem de carácter, culto e requintado nos gostos. Em jovem aderiu aos ideais do Liberalismo e foi obrigado, por seu pai, a sair de casa e a instalar-se em Inglaterra. Após o pai falecer regressa a Lisboa para casar com Maria Eduarda Runa, mas pouco tempo depois escolhe o exílio por razões de ordem política. Há em Os Maias um retrato da Lisboa da epóca. Carlos, que mora na Rua das Janelas Verdes, caminha com frequência até ao Rossio (embora, por vezes, vá a cavalo ou de carruagem). Algumas das lojas citadas no livro ainda existem - a Casa Havaneza, no Chiado, por exemplo. É possível seguir os diferentes percursos de Carlos ou do Ega pelas suas da Baixa lisboeta, ainda que algumas tenham mudado de nome. No final do livro, quando Carlos volta a Lisboa muitos anos depois, somos levados a ver as novidades - a Avenida da Liberdade, que substituiu o Passeio Público, e que é descrita como uma coisa nova, e feia pela sua novidade, exactamente como nos anos 70 se falava das casas de emigrante. O romance veicula sobre o país uma perspectiva muito derrotista, muito pessimista. Tirando a natureza (o Tejo, Sintra, Santa Olávia...), é tudo uma choldra ignóbil. Predomina uma visão de estrangeirado, de quem só valoriza as civilizações superiores - da França e Inglaterra, principalmente. Os políticos são mesquinhos, ignorantes ou corruptos (Gouvarinho, Sousa Neto...); os homens das Letras sao boémios e dissolutos, retrógrados ou distantes da realidade concreta (Alencar, Ega...: lembre-se o que se passou no Sarau do Teatro da Trindade); os jornalistas boémios e venais (Palma...); os homens do desporto não conseguem organizar uma corrida de cavalos, pois não há hipódromo à altura, nem cavalos, nem cavaleiros, as pessoas não vestem como o evento exigia, as senhoras traziam vestidos de missa. Para cúmulo de tudo isto, os protagonistas acabam vencidos da vida. Apesar de ser isto referido no fim do livro, pode-se ver que ainda há alguma esperanca implícita, nas passagens em que Carlos da Maia e João da Ega dizem que o apetite humano é a causa de todos os seus problemas e que portanto nunca mais terão apetites, mas logo a seguir dizem que lhes está a apetecer um &quot;prato de paio com ervilhas,&quot; ou quando dizem que a pressa não leva a nada e que a vida deve ser levada com calma mas começam a correr para apanhar o americano (eléctrico). Mais do que crítica de costumes, o romance mostra-nos um país - sobretudo Lisboa - que se dissolve, incapaz de se regenerar. Quando o autor escreve mais tarde A Cidade e as Serras, expõe uma atitude muito mais construtiva: o protagonista regenera-se pela descoberta das raízes rurais ancestrais não atingidas pela degradação da civilização, num movimento inverso ao que predomina n\'Os Maias.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"11543393728670501825\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n //<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_1092477'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1092477.A_Cidade_e_as_Serras?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">A Cidade e as Serras<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/6913270.E_a_de_Queir_s?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Eça de Queirós<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.74 avg rating &mdash; 5,552 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1901\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer11395376449253857316\">Biblioteca Ulisseia de Autores Portugueses #5\n\nJosé Maria de Eça de Queiroz (Póvoa de Varzim, 25 de novembro de 1845 — Neuilly-sur-Seine, 16 de agosto de 1900), escritor e ensaísta, foi um dos nomes mais importantes da literatura portuguesa. De nome <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText11395376449253857316\" style=\"display:none\">Biblioteca Ulisseia de Autores Portugueses #5\n\nJosé Maria de Eça de Queiroz (Póvoa de Varzim, 25 de novembro de 1845 — Neuilly-sur-Seine, 16 de agosto de 1900), escritor e ensaísta, foi um dos nomes mais importantes da literatura portuguesa. De nome completo José Maria de Eça de Queirós nasceu a Novembro de 1845, numa casa na Praça do Almada, em Póvoa de Varzim. O seu pai, José Maria de Almeida de Teixeira de Queirós, nascido no Brasil e vindo para Portugal com um ano de idade, provinha de uma família de magistrados perseguidos pelos seus ideais liberais que defendiam uma doutrina constitucional. Eça foi internado no Colégio da Lapa, no Porto, de onde saiu em 1861, com dezasseis anos, para a Universidade de Coimbra, onde estudou Direito. Num ambiente boémio da cidade universitária de Coimbra estes jovens reuniam-se para trocar ideias, livros e formas para renovar a vida política e cultural portuguesa, que estava a viver uma autêntica revolução social com a introdução dos novos meios de transportes ferroviários que traziam, todos os dias, novidades do centro da Europa, influenciando esta geração para novas ideologias e valores. Foi nesse grupo que Eça conheceu os futuros escritores e poetas, Teófilo Braga, Ramalho Ortigão, Guerra Junqueiro, Guilherme de Azevedo, Oliveira Martins, entre outros; mas sobretudo, foi aí que travou amizade com Antero de Quental, um jovem carismático a quem os membros do grupo chamavam de líder e que incentivou os restantes a seguir e a difundir as então recentes correntes ideológicas e literárias europeias: o Positivismo, o Socialismo e o Realismo-Naturalismo. Notabilizou-se pela originalidade e riqueza do seu estilo e linguagem, nomeadamente pelo realismo descritivo e pela crítica social constantes nos seus romances mas, tal como o crítico literário, Jacinto Prado Coelho disse: &quot;foi mais analista social do que psicólogo; ironizou Portugal porque muito o amava e o queria melhor.&quot;<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"11395376449253857316\" Pedi aos contemporâneos que o conheceram notícias e miudezas, a fim de entrar de consciência naquele trabalho. Escrevi o romance em quinze dias, os mais atormentados de minha vida. Tão horrorizada tenho deles a memória, que nunca mais abrirei o «Amor de Perdição», nem lhe passarei a lima sobre os defeitos nas edições futuras, se é que não saiu tolhiço incorrigível da primeira. Movia-me à desconfiança o ser ele triste, sem interpolação de risos, sombrio, e rematado por catástrofe de confranger o ânimo dos leitores, que se interessam na boa sorte de uns, e no castigo de outros personagens. Em honra e louvor das pessoas que estimaram o meu livro, confessarei agradavelmente que julguei mal delas. […] O livro agradou como está. Além disso,<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText16326627159164352904\" style=\"display:none\">É a história de amizade entre um rapaz e uma Menina. Ela vive no mar, e é bailarina da &quot;Grande Raia&quot;, uma rainha dos mares, que sobre ela mantém vigilância, não a deixando realizar o seu sonho de conhecer a terra firme, onde mora o rapaz. Além disso, a menina não consegue sobreviver longe da água, pois, fica desidratada, ainda que consiga respirar dentro e fora de água. O rapaz, com que estabelece amizade, tem o desejo de conhecer o fundo do mar. A história desenrola-se com a tentativa dos dois em realizar os seus sonhos.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"16326627159164352904\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div class=\'wtrButtonContainer wtrSignedOut\' id=\'25_book_6480073\'>\n<div class=\'wtrUp wtrLeft\'>\n<form action=\"/shelf/add_to_shelf\"       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/25322.Miguel_Sousa_Tavares">About Miguel Sousa Tavares</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/25322.Miguel_Sousa_Tavares"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1458080596p3/25322.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/25322.Miguel_Sousa_Tavares">Miguel Sousa Tavares
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
344
followers
</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7809740247191228092">Miguel Sousa Tavares is a portuguese journalist and was born in Porto, on the 25th June 1952. His mother, Sophia de Mello Breyner, was a poetess and his father, Francisco de Sousa Tavares, a lawyer and a journalist. After taking the Law course, he carried advocacy during twelve years, but left it permanently to become a full time journalist.<br/>He first appeared at television in 1978, by entering the </span>
  <span id="freeText7809740247191228092" style="display:none">Miguel Sousa Tavares is a portuguese journalist and was born in Porto, on the 25th June 1952. His mother, Sophia de Mello Breyner, was a poetess and his father, Francisco de Sousa Tavares, a lawyer and a journalist. After taking the Law course, he carried advocacy during twelve years, but left it permanently to become a full time journalist.<br />He first appeared at television in 1978, by entering the <i>Radiotelevisão Portuguesa</i> channel (<i>Portuguese Radiotelevision</i>).<br />In 1989, he was one of the creators of <i>Grande Reportagem</i> magazine (<i>Big Report</i>) and he became director of it in 1990, place where he settled during ten years. He also published some chronics and wrote to the journal <i>Público</i> (<i>Public</i>) from 1990 until 2002. At the same time, he also wrote chronics in other publications such as <i>A Bola</i> (<i>The Ball</i>, a sport journal), <i>Máxima</i> (<i>Maximum</i>, a female magazine) and in the online journal <i>Diário Digital</i> (<i>Digital Diary</i>).<br />He worked at SIC, a private TV channel, where he hosted information programmes such as "Crossfire". He left SIC and refused the invitation to be general director of RTP but, in 1999, he returned to the television.<br />He entered TVI in 1999 where he hosted the programme <i>Legítima Defesa</i> (<i>Self Defense</i>) and in 2000 he started to work as a fixed commentator at the <i>Jornal Nacional</i> (<i>Nacional Journal</i>, in TVI).<br />He also released various books, and almost all of them are chronics. The first one, <i>Sahara, a República da Areia</i> (<i>Sahara, the Sand Republic</i>), was edited in 1985 and was part of a report. Ten years later he wrote a collection of political texts called <i>Um Nómada no Oásis</i> (<i>A Nomadic in the Oasis</i>) and <i>O Segredo do Rio</i> (<i>The Secret of the River</i>, a children story). In 1998, the book called <i>Sul</i> (<i>South</i>) came out and in 2001 the book called <i> Não te Deixarei Morrrer, David Crockett</i> (<i>I won't let you die, David Crockett</i>). In this last year, was also edited <i>Anos Perdidos</i> (<i>Lost Years</i>), a colection of chronics dedicated to the govern of António Guterres.<br />His first novel was <i>Equador</i> (<i>Equator</i>), first edited in 2003 and which sold more than 370 thousand copies. This novel was so sucessful that posteriorly was released in Brazil, Germany, Spain, Latin America, Czech Republic and the Netherlands, and also won the 25th edition of the Grinzane Cavour prize for the best foreign novel of the year, in Italy. In October of 2007, Miguel Sousa Tavares released <i>Rio das Flores</i> (<i>River of Flowers</i>), also a success. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7809740247191228092" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
